<span id="freeTextContainer15039083014402854586">In a series of crimes that has stunned Washington, D.C., bank robbers have been laying out precise demands when they enter the building — and then killing the bank employees and their families if those instructions are not followed to the letter.<br />Detective Alex Cross takes on the case, certain that this is no ordinary bank robber at work — the pathological need for control</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15039083014402854586">In a series of crimes that has stunned Washington, D.C., bank robbers have been laying out precise demands when they enter the building — and then killing the bank employees and their families if those instructions are not followed to the letter.<br />Detective Alex Cross takes on the case, certain that this is no ordinary bank robber at work — the pathological need for control and perfection is too great. Cross is in the midst of a personal crisis at home, but the case becomes all-consuming as he learns that the Mastermind is plotting one huge, last, perfect crime.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/571549438?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 26, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2446219-jessica" class="user" title="Jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer571549438">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14827151684507369363">Ugh. I've read a handful of Patterson's books and none of them would qualify as good literature, but this one was particularly awful. The writing is cliched and one-dimensional, the characters are uninteresting, and the story tries to be so shocking that it actually ends up being predictable. There are not enough clues to actually figure out who the bad guy is, so basically you just have to wait until they tell you and then you aren't surprised and don't care. I didn't care when his girlfriend l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14827151684507369363">Ugh. I've read a handful of Patterson's books and none of them would qualify as good literature, but this one was particularly awful. The writing is cliched and one-dimensional, the characters are uninteresting, and the story tries to be so shocking that it actually ends up being predictable. There are not enough clues to actually figure out who the bad guy is, so basically you just have to wait until they tell you and then you aren't surprised and don't care. I didn't care when his girlfriend left, I didn't care when one of the main characters died because there is just no reason to care. Didn't care when his daughter had a brain tumor, in fact the kids were so unrealistic in how sweet and happy they were that every scene with them was more laughable than serious. I really don't understand why these books are so popular other than that the majority of people are practically illiterate. I have nothing against violence and murder and shocking stories, but at least make them interesting.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14827151684507369363">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_134593231">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134593231" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4187864-david-erickson" class="left imgcol" title="David Erickson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1366644070p2/4187864.jpg" alt="David Erickson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/134593231?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 11, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4187864-david-erickson" class="user" title="David Erickson">David Erickson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer134593231">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2195570196376721025">I felt this wasn't the best of the Alex Cross series, but it was very good. The wirting pattern makes it easy to set the book down and come back to it.<br /><br />The one thing that annoys me is that the biggest bad guy never seems to get his nailed. While in some of the books, some of the bad guys are figured out and brought to justice, but dang I want to see the worst of the worst - the mastermind - nailed. I know this makes it possible for a same theme sequel, but it leaves an unsatisfactory aftertaste.<br /><br />I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2195570196376721025">I felt this wasn't the best of the Alex Cross series, but it was very good. The wirting pattern makes it easy to set the book down and come back to it.<br /><br />The one thing that annoys me is that the biggest bad guy never seems to get his nailed. While in some of the books, some of the bad guys are figured out and brought to justice, but dang I want to see the worst of the worst - the mastermind - nailed. I know this makes it possible for a same theme sequel, but it leaves an unsatisfactory aftertaste.<br /><br />I purposely purchased 'Violets are Blue' to see Alex catch the mastermind, but in looking up the novel, I discovered that he once again eludes capture. Then I learn the Weasel is still at large too. As Alex Cross says, he's in an ongoing nightmare he can't seem to shake, but us readers deserve a break too. Alex nails the current bad guys, but the really bad guys, the ones who torment him, never get caught.<br /><br />I'm not sure I'm going to pick up the sequel to "Violets are Blue'. It's way past time for Patterson to let Alex finally nail the Weasel and the Mastermind and move on. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2195570196376721025">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/3690472-thom-swennes" class="user" title="Thom Swennes">Thom Swennes</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer327442223">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1614228118233183435">Generally I like books to have complete stories. These stories have a beginning, middle and end and when I read the last page my mind evaluates or digests what I have read and I can then form an opinion. Roses are Red by James Patterson isn’t like his average stories. Most of Patterson’s novels begin by corralling the reader into his world and leading them down corridors with short chapters and never ending action. Along this fast paced ride through the hall of suspense the reader gets flash imp</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1614228118233183435">Generally I like books to have complete stories. These stories have a beginning, middle and end and when I read the last page my mind evaluates or digests what I have read and I can then form an opinion. Roses are Red by James Patterson isn’t like his average stories. Most of Patterson’s novels begin by corralling the reader into his world and leading them down corridors with short chapters and never ending action. Along this fast paced ride through the hall of suspense the reader gets flash impressions of possible danger in different directions as through open doors and unfettered windows. This, eventually, leads the reader to a climax that gets the heart pumping and juices flowing. When the story comes to an end a feeling of wellbeing fills your mind and the world is once again a good and safe place. Roses are Red is different. An extensive and exhausting manhunt lasting four hundred pages ends where it began (minus a few cold victims) and the reader can start again in its sequel. It has all the elements of a memorable read and I highly recommend it to lovers of crime fiction. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1614228118233183435">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75331454" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2703484-kevin-wijas" class="left imgcol" title="Kevin Wijas"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Kevin Wijas" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/75331454?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 21, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2703484-kevin-wijas" class="user" title="Kevin Wijas">Kevin Wijas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer75331454">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10973667137658081415">Roses are Red by James Patterson is an exciting mystery that is led by D.C’s top detective Alex Cross. A group of professional bank robbers and their leader “The Mastermind” plan and execute perfect robberies while committing malicious murders of “innocent” people. Crosses life is a mess throughout the book as he deals with family problems while trying to stop the craziest psychopath he has every seen. This book is not only a great read but it also shows the importance of family life and how qui</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10973667137658081415">Roses are Red by James Patterson is an exciting mystery that is led by D.C’s top detective Alex Cross. A group of professional bank robbers and their leader “The Mastermind” plan and execute perfect robberies while committing malicious murders of “innocent” people. Crosses life is a mess throughout the book as he deals with family problems while trying to stop the craziest psychopath he has every seen. This book is not only a great read but it also shows the importance of family life and how quickly someone can be on the edge of dieing. It makes you realize how much you should cherish life and enjoy every minutes of it. James Patterson is an exciting author who makes reading become more of a movie in your head. His easy to read style of writing and his suspenseful scenes makes you feel as if you’re following the book through a video camera. “He dived off the deck-which was five floors above the street”… “Francis had made a dive five stories down to a shimmery blue swimming pool”(Page 362). He draws pictures in your head from everything from crazy murderers to his valued family situations. I could never put this book down since from chapter to chapter I couldn’t predict what was going to happen next. The only down side to this book was that some times I felt like the characters did things that put them in danger that could have been easily avoided if they had used common sense. If you’re a Law and Order or CSI crime lover, then this book is definitely for you. It doesn’t matter whether you’re fourteen or fifty, Patterson writes in a way so that anyone can enjoy it as long as you love a good mystery. So if you are an action junkie who loves unpredictable twist and turns, then Roses are Red is without a doubt a great book for you. I would give it 5 stars out of five. This book is an absolute thriller and roller coaster right up to the end. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10973667137658081415">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer97653076">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18095580517058975215">This book is about a man named Alex Cross, who is a homicide detective, who recently saved his beloved, from a mass murderer named, Weasel. In the book, Alex Cross comes across a new case, where a so called, "Mastermind," robs banks and kills all the hostages. As he investigates the case, he recently breaks up with his beloved, and is depressed. One of Alex Cross's main external conflicts, is for him to find the Mastermind and send him to jail. One of his internal conflicts, is him trying to fin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18095580517058975215">This book is about a man named Alex Cross, who is a homicide detective, who recently saved his beloved, from a mass murderer named, Weasel. In the book, Alex Cross comes across a new case, where a so called, "Mastermind," robs banks and kills all the hostages. As he investigates the case, he recently breaks up with his beloved, and is depressed. One of Alex Cross's main external conflicts, is for him to find the Mastermind and send him to jail. One of his internal conflicts, is him trying to find a new beloved.<br /><br />I came across a connection in the book. When Alex Cross learns about<br />the Mastermind, this reminds me of how everday in the world, people are getting robbed, killed and all other kinds of stuff. I think people need to start realizing that, your life is basically over if you kill someone. If you kill somebody, its going to affect you in the long run.<br /><br />I would give this book 4 stars, because it was a very good book about romance, drama, and action. But I never felt any vibe. I thought in some parts, the book was boring and other parts the book was amazing. I would reccomend this book to anyone, who loves books, about homicide detectives.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer398728188">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1841699804595234212">Unfortunately, this is going to be my last James Patterson novel. I think that there just comes a point where you realize you have outgrow certain authors and I haven't particularly cared for the last three Patterson novels I have read. Sad to me, because I remember staying up ALL NIGHT to read <a title="Kiss the Girls (Alex Cross, #2) by James Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13148.Kiss_the_Girls__Alex_Cross___2_">Kiss the Girls</a> in college. I realized tonight that I don't want to read any more JP and I don't want to read any more John Grisham, so all of the rest of my unread novels of both of these guys (great writ</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1841699804595234212">Unfortunately, this is going to be my last James Patterson novel. I think that there just comes a point where you realize you have outgrow certain authors and I haven't particularly cared for the last three Patterson novels I have read. Sad to me, because I remember staying up ALL NIGHT to read <a title="Kiss the Girls (Alex Cross, #2) by James Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13148.Kiss_the_Girls__Alex_Cross___2_">Kiss the Girls</a> in college. I realized tonight that I don't want to read any more JP and I don't want to read any more John Grisham, so all of the rest of my unread novels of both of these guys (great writers that they are) are going to be going to other readers that want them via paperbackswap.com. How did I come to this conclusion? I really wasn't that razzed about this novel at all and I'm shocked that it was a best seller. First you think it's one guy, and it's not. Then you think it's another guy...and it's not. And the final shocking crime? Yeah, it's pretty bad, no question, but there are so many unanswered questions. The romance between Alex and Betsey was sweet, and maybe I would have been more emotionally vested in the Christine/baby Alex situation if I had read <a title="Pop Goes the Weasel (Alex Cross, #5) by James Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13143.Pop_Goes_the_Weasel__Alex_Cross___5_">Pop Goes the Weasel</a>, but that set aside (the fact that these Cross books should be read in order), this book just didn't rely a lot on evidence to follow the Mastermind (I guess because there wasn't much), the crimes all seemed to be the same with no real MO or pattern or differentiation, and really? I seriously could have lived without the necrophilia. The end didn't shock me one bit...again, another curse of reading this book out of the series order. But as a stand-alone book, it just didn't hold my attention very well. Sayonara, Dr. Cross. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1841699804595234212">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2345490593893092671">A couple of friends have been recommending Patterson to me for ages, so when I saw this and the sequel - Violets are Blue - together in a charity shop i picked up the pair. Patterson writes in short, punchy chapters and vivid detail, and i flew through the book, pulled forward by the pace. It was, however, an entirely unsatisfying experience. The writing is incredibly formulaic - detective battling personal problems? check. the only man who can solve the case? check? increasing complications in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2345490593893092671">A couple of friends have been recommending Patterson to me for ages, so when I saw this and the sequel - Violets are Blue - together in a charity shop i picked up the pair. Patterson writes in short, punchy chapters and vivid detail, and i flew through the book, pulled forward by the pace. It was, however, an entirely unsatisfying experience. The writing is incredibly formulaic - detective battling personal problems? check. the only man who can solve the case? check? increasing complications in his life? check.<br /><br />Turning the last page, confronted with the twist and cliffhanger ending, I found I had absolutely no interest in the characters or how things turned out, so both books went right back to the charity shop.<br /><br />Perhaps this isn't representative of Patterson's work but, given the rate he churns them out, I suspect it is, and this left me with no interest in investigating his books further.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5343902916373946121">Amy and I found this book by the curb in a town in Germany, and picked it up on a whim. After reading the first chapter (4 pages, maybe 1000 words, probably less), we both put it down because it has such an unbelievably unpromising start.             Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=james-patterson" class="actionLinkLite">james-patterson</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer277994912659363058">ROSES ARE RED is of roughly the same literary quality as a Harlequin romance; even still, it's the best Alex Cross novel (up to this point) since KISS THE GIRLS. Finally, we get a bad guy who's actually somewhat interesting and can give Cross a run for his money. Story-wise, the book is entertaining enough...if you can get past Patterson's frequently abysmal writing.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer738723989">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer550302275003341625">James Patterson's Roses Are Red depicts a detective in Washington D.C. who is on the case of multiple bank robbery/murders around the area. At first they seem like simple jobs gone wrong but patterns soon appear getting the FBI involved. Many hostages are being murdered leaving no margin for error. It is written in third person limited letting really grasp Alex's (the main character) thoughts. Alex goes through many disasters throughout that tear him apart. <br />Before I read this book I was not a bi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText550302275003341625">James Patterson's Roses Are Red depicts a detective in Washington D.C. who is on the case of multiple bank robbery/murders around the area. At first they seem like simple jobs gone wrong but patterns soon appear getting the FBI involved. Many hostages are being murdered leaving no margin for error. It is written in third person limited letting really grasp Alex's (the main character) thoughts. Alex goes through many disasters throughout that tear him apart. <br />Before I read this book I was not a big fan of murder mysteries but now I can see why so many people love them. One of the main reasons is that I love the way James Patterson writes. He creates such a vivid picture in your mind for every scene. The strong parts of this book would definitely be the shocking moments that you'd never expect to happen. I would no doubt recommend this book to a friend or student. Next chance I get I am reading one of the other books in the series.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer834013524">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12806952548242492958">I try not to judge a book by comparing it to other books I've read. I try to judge based on how it met or exceeded my expectations. This is the first Patterson book I've read, and based on what I had heard from fans of his, I didn't expect high literature, but I did expect a simply written, well-crafted mystery. Suffice to say, I was very under-whelmed. It was an interesting enough story to keep me reading until the end, but the writing was full of painful cliches, one dimensional characters, an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12806952548242492958">I try not to judge a book by comparing it to other books I've read. I try to judge based on how it met or exceeded my expectations. This is the first Patterson book I've read, and based on what I had heard from fans of his, I didn't expect high literature, but I did expect a simply written, well-crafted mystery. Suffice to say, I was very under-whelmed. It was an interesting enough story to keep me reading until the end, but the writing was full of painful cliches, one dimensional characters, and groan-worthy attempts at cleverness. For such a successful author, Patterson isn't a very good writer. It was a quick an easy read, and there is a possibility I will give ol' James another shot in the future, but for now, I've had enough. </span>

  <a href="/user/show/20380501-maggie-james" class="left imgcol" title="Maggie James"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1369900821p2/20380501.jpg" alt="Maggie James" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/828118613?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 25, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20380501-maggie-james" class="user" title="Maggie James">Maggie James</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/20380501-maggie-james?shelf=crime" class="actionLinkLite">crime</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer828118613">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8867950086734983239">Hmm, maybe I've read too many pulp James Patterson books. Normally they're OK and deliver a quick dose of easy entertainment, and this one was no exception. There did seem to be a lot of unanswered questions at the end, though, which I suspect might get answered in his book 'Violets Are Blue'. This doesn't sit well with me - I don't want to have to read a subsequent book to get answers to what happens. </span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1292057773">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1292057773" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/23859411-megan-k" class="left imgcol" title="Megan K"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Megan K" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1292057773?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 28, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/23859411-megan-k" class="user" title="Megan K">Megan K</a>

          added it




        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1292057773">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10089478802666867747"> James Patterson has always been a favorite author of mine, and I had my bar set high when I first opened the front cover of Roses are Red. In fact, the first part of the first sentence had me hooked; “Brianne Parker didn’t look like a bank robber or a murderer --” (3). Who wouldn’t want to read on? Unfortunately, I fell into this trap. <br /> Roses are Red is a story about Alex Cross, a highly respected homicide detective, who also happens to be the loving father of two children. Killers are on the l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10089478802666867747">	James Patterson has always been a favorite author of mine, and I had my bar set high when I first opened the front cover of Roses are Red. In fact, the first part of the first sentence had me hooked; “Brianne Parker didn’t look like a bank robber or a murderer --” (3). Who wouldn’t want to read on? Unfortunately, I fell into this trap. <br />	Roses are Red is a story about Alex Cross, a highly respected homicide detective, who also happens to be the loving father of two children. Killers are on the loose, robbing banks and killing anyone that gets in their way. These murderers have even gone as far as taking the tellers’ families hostage and killing them if need be. As a family man, Cross can feel the pain of the innocent victims. Murder after murder after murder takes place, showing no specific pattern or reasoning. <br />	Little did Alex Cross know, him and his partner were high up on the hitlist of the criminal, which they refer to as the “Mastermind”. This affected him intensely when he found out; if he can’t even protect himself, how on earth would he be able to protect his family? Cross’s mindset immediately did a 180 when he went from putting himself first, to putting his family’s safety first. This was clearly the most expected “plot twist” there is. The good guy goes from caring about him to caring about everyone else, then he gets killed, la la la. . . but in the end, his family is safe, and everyone is okay. Right?<br />	Sadly, it takes forever to get to this point in the book. In fact, the pacing of the book is so slow, that I was tempted to put down a James Patterson book, which are words that shouldn’t even be found in the same sentence for me. I was immensely disappointed by this book. I had high expectations, and the quality of the writing didn’t even reach half of my hopes. Dialogue was boring and unnatural, pacing was slow, and the same repetitive robberies and murders take place the entire time. If you are a person that loves books that are slow, boring and life-dragging, I have definitely found the novel for you. This book really wasn’t my speed, but the average for Patterson’s overall writing that I have read is only brought down slightly, and I would still recommend any of his other books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10089478802666867747">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/19200150-david-roberts" class="user" title="David Roberts">David Roberts</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer922656436">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5232504370843279951">I am reviewing the thriller Roses Are Red by James Patterson which is an excellent novel which I bought from a car boot sale. It is part of the Alex Cross series about a psychologist who works for the police and solves mostly serial killings. The killer in this book and I think he appeared in one of the other books in the series is called the Mastermind and Patterson did say in an interview he is the most frightening baddie in any of his books. He robs places like banks where he tells the staff</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5232504370843279951">I am reviewing the thriller Roses Are Red by James Patterson which is an excellent novel which I bought from a car boot sale. It is part of the Alex Cross series about a psychologist who works for the police and solves mostly serial killings. The killer in this book and I think he appeared in one of the other books in the series is called the Mastermind and Patterson did say in an interview he is the most frightening baddie in any of his books. He robs places like banks where he tells the staff people close to them are being held hostage and will die along with them if the robbery doesn't get done in a set period of time. He then kills the people are rather his cohortd do for the fun of it. In the one robbery he has someone lock two of the people in the safe of the bank. and their families get murdeed because he knows its impossible to rob the bank in that allotted time and it has been carefully rehearsed. Alex has to work with a sexy FBI agent and his partner who got kidnapped in a previous novel as part of her therapy from the trauma decides she must leave him. His nanny looks after most of his children and one of his children must be treated for a tumor. There are lots of twists and turns in the story and one problem is the Mastermind rarely carries out the crimes himself but has people working for him that do which makes it very difficult to catch him. He does rape a lady and tries to force her to have his baby and of course not report it and has her poisoned when she doesn't go through with it. They do keep arresting people thinking they are him only to be disappointed. There is one part where he has a coach hijacked and uses one of the nuclear missile silos in the area to shield it from the heat seeking helicopter. This story is probably not for the more squeamish but is one of the better installments in the Alex Cross series. It would make a good film. </span>

      <a href="/user/show/3426724-chucklesthescot" class="user" title="chucklesthescot">chucklesthescot</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">thriller fans</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=mystery-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3426724-chucklesthescot?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer93864587">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2714104047921161402">Mastermind is the new killer on the block. He sends teams of bank robbers to abduct and brutally murder people during the crimes and the violence is getting worse by every case. Alex is already struggling with losing Christine and his baby from his life and this case nearly pushes him over the edge.<br /> It wasn't the best book in the series but I was left totally gobsmacked by the ending and the identity of the Mastermind. Hats off to you Mr Patterson, I never saw that one coming! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1052756290">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4046049455803661792">Ho appena saputo che James Patterson è l’autore più venduto nel mondo e che su ogni 10 libri acquistati nel mondo, uno è suo. Sono terribilmente dispiaciuto poiché, mi rendo conto, ho contribuito non poco ad abbassare le statistiche di questo signore. Nella mia ben fornita libreria, Mastermind è il suo primo romanzo e probabilmente resterà anche l’unico.<br />Temo che adesso dovrò anche spiegarne il perché. Di primo acchito, mi verrebbe da dire che JP è la versione maschile di Patricia Cornwell. L’int</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4046049455803661792">Ho appena saputo che James Patterson è l’autore più venduto nel mondo e che su ogni 10 libri acquistati nel mondo, uno è suo. Sono terribilmente dispiaciuto poiché, mi rendo conto, ho contribuito non poco ad abbassare le statistiche di questo signore. Nella mia ben fornita libreria, Mastermind è il suo primo romanzo e probabilmente resterà anche l’unico.<br />Temo che adesso dovrò anche spiegarne il perché. Di primo acchito, mi verrebbe da dire che JP è la versione maschile di Patricia Cornwell. L’intera storia è, per dirla con un termine anglosassone che rende perfettamente l’idea, one-dimensional. I personaggi mancano totalmente di caratterizzazione e l’attenzione dell’autore è rivolta unicamente alla vicenda che si snoda con l’unico obiettivo di scioccare il lettore ad ogni pagina. Obiettivo difficile da perseguire tanto che, alla fine, più che scioccare riesce solo nell’intento diametralmente opposto di essere prevedibile. <br />Ma sono i personaggi il vero lato negativo di questo romanzo. Emblematica la figura dei due figli di Alex Cross, detective dalle costanti decisioni sbagliate e i cui amori sono perseguitati da una sfiga senza fine. A dirla tutta, fossi una donna, mi guarderei bene dall’innamorarmi di Alex Cross. Io ci tengo alla mia vita!<br />Dicevo dei figli adolescenti di Cross. La figlia, dodicenne se ricordo bene, affetta da un tumore al cervello parla e si comporta con una maturità totalmente irrealistica. Appare così dolce e felice da rendere ogni scena che la concerne semplicemente ridicola. Il fratellino, ancora più piccolo, non è da meno e contribuisce a ridicolizzare ancora di più l’insieme familiare di Alex Cross. A ben vedere, l’unica parvenza di credibilità è di Nana Mama (eccezione fatta per il nome assurdo) che, da buona nonna, è l’unico personaggio dell’intera storia ad apparire veritiero.<br />Stendo un velo pietoso su tutto il resto del parco personaggi. Non riesco a salvarne uno solo, Cross compreso.<br />La storia, invece, è ben congegnata e vale al libro la seconda stellina. Mi fermo lì, dato che JP si macchia di un altro peccato mortale. Si è dimenticato, nel variopinto parco personaggi, di includere almeno un altro candidato credibile alla colpevolezza. L’identità dell’assassino è talmente ovvia da risultare stucchevole. E non perché il lettore lo capisca in una sfida all’autore dove riesca a scovare indizi che ne indichino la colpevolezza (del resto JP non ne mette e l’identità dell’assassino appare come il coniglio dal cappello senza che JP si degni di spiegare perché Mastermind sia diventato Mastermind). Si va semplicemente a esclusione. Non poteva essere nessun altro. Tra l’altro, JP si dimentica di spiegare come, perché e ogni altra cosa voi vogliate sapere. Si limita a dirvi l’identità di Mastermind, lasciando il lettore con la sensazione di essere stato preso in giro.<br />Credetemi, se amate i thriller, allora in giro c’è di molto meglio.?<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4046049455803661792">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1397652898712826117">A solid addition to the Alex Cross Series.... This is the first of a 2 parter..<br /><br />Cross's nemesis refers to himself as The Mastermind ! You keep waiting for the bozo to choke on his title but then you realize that It is Not Hubris and the title is Well Deserved...<br /><br />There is only one main storyline and that is rare in the Cross Series. That also helps in keeping everything focused. This book succeeds on doing the little things right and staying on point. <br />Good book to read....</span>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3780.James_Patterson">About James Patterson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3780.James_Patterson"><img alt="3780" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1284492096p2/3780.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer10162354426663395680"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.com">Offical US Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk">Offical UK Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespattersonya.com">Offical James Patterson Young Adult Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.middleschoolbook.com">Offical Site for James Patterson's Middle School Series</a><br /><br /><br /><br />The subject of a <em>Time</em> magazine feature called, "The Man Who Can't Miss," James Patterson is the bestselling author of the past year, bar none, with more than 16 million books sold in North America alone. In 2007, one of every fifteen hardcover fiction books sold was a Patter</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10162354426663395680"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.com">Offical US Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk">Offical UK Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespattersonya.com">Offical James Patterson Young Adult Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.middleschoolbook.com">Offical Site for James Patterson's Middle School Series</a><br /><br /><br /><br />The subject of a <em>Time</em> magazine feature called, "The Man Who Can't Miss," James Patterson is the bestselling author of the past year, bar none, with more than 16 million books sold in North America alone. In 2007, one of every fifteen hardcover fiction books sold was a Patterson title. In the past three years, James has sold more books than any other author (according to Bookscan), and in total, James's books have sold an estimated 220 million copies worldwide. He is the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on <em>The New York Times</em> adult and children's lists and is the only author to have five new hardcover novels debut at #1 on the list in one year—a record-breaking feat he's accomplished every year since 2005. To date, James Patterson has had nineteen consecutive #1 <em>New York Times</em> bestselling novels, and holds the <em>New York Times</em> record for most Hardcover Fiction bestselling titles by a single author (63 total), which is also a Guinness World Record.<br /><br /><br /><br />From his James Patterson Pageturner Awards (which rewarded groups and individuals for creative and effective ways to spread the joy of reading) to his website <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.readkiddoread.com">ReadKiddoRead.com</a> (which helps adults find books that kids are sure to love) to his regular donations of thousands of books to troops overseas, Patterson is a lifelong champion of books and reading. His first foray into books for all ages was the critically acclaimed Maximum Ride series, which debuted on the New York Times bestsellers list at #1 and remained there for twelve straight weeks. The series has so far made appearances on <em>The New York Times</em> bestsellers lists ninety-four cumulative times, proving that kids of all ages love page turners. He captured the attention of boy readers with the Daniel X series, and his third series for readers of all ages debuted in December 2009 with <em>Witch &amp; Wizard</em>, which spent five consecutive weeks atop the <em>New York Times</em> bestsellers list.<br /><br /><br /><br />Patterson is the creator of the #1 new detective series of the past dozen years, featuring Alex Cross and including the Hollywood-adapted "Along Came a Spider" and "Kiss the Girls," starring Academy Award-winning actor Morgan Freeman. He is also the creator of the #1 new detective series of the past five years, featuring Lindsay Boxer and the other members of the Women's Murder Club, from which the ABC television drama series was adapted. He has authored books behind six films on the Hollywood fast-track, including the upcoming Maximum Ride movie forthcoming from Avi Arad, the producer of X-Men and Spiderman.<br /><br /><br /><br />He is the author of novels—from The Thomas Berryman Number (1976) to Honeymoon (2005)—that have won awards including the Edgar, the BCA Mystery Guild's Thriller of the Year, the International Thriller of the Year award, and the Reader's Digest Reader's Choice Award. And, he has won a Children's Choice Book Council's Children's Choice Awards "Author of the Year" award (2010).<br /><br /><br /><br />One of Forbes magazine's Celebrity 100, James made a guest appearance on the popular FOX TV show "The Simpsons" in March, 2007.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10162354426663395680">...more</a>

    </div>
